### Post by Mark76 on 2009-03-01
(Blatantly plagarised from the previous month's screenshot thread)

 March 2009 screenshot thread
March 2009 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
* To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

Sticky me :D

### Post by Mark76 on 2009-03-01
DIY Thumbnails

Run scrot with the following argument. -t or --thumb NUM (where NUM is a percentage of the original size).  I think something like 20 would be a good place to start for most screens.  You can also use a -d or --delay set to whatever value you like if you want to minimise the terminal (assuming you're using a terminal) before the shot is taken.

Upload both versions (full size and thumb) to your favourite image hosting site.

In the reply options select Insert link and paste the direct link to your full sized screenshot in the dialog box. 

Then click on Insert Image and paste the direct link to your thumb in that dialog box (the Image link should be embedded inside the url link)

Voila! A thumbnail that opens up the full sized image

### Post by sertse on 2009-03-01
I admit, I pose. ;) Taking screenshots again and again till I think it's right. lol

Background: Surreal Sunset - [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Surreal+Sunset+%2BBlue+%2BHuman+Colors?content=85183](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Surreal+Sunset+%2BBlue+%2BHuman+Colors?content=85183)

There's also a matching GDM theme - [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Sunset?content=85709](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Sunset?content=85709)

GTK theme: Clearlooks

Icon theme: Gartoon Redux [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Gartoon+Redux?content=74841](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Gartoon+Redux?content=74841)

Fluxbox theme: Bora Blue

"Wbar" is the dock/launcher on top. "Stalonetray" is the system tray on the top right. Stalonetray is also used to stop maximised apps covering wbar, a common problem amongst wbar/fluxbox users. :)

### Post by Piraja on 2009-03-01
Two of my laptop desktops (a.k.a. workspaces) atm: Openbox, Exaile, Conky, a modified GTK theme, and &#8212; last but not least &#8212; Nautilus not behaving badly this time but browsing files on my remote desktop machine (on the left side screenshot).

Finally found [instructions]("http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/topic/84/using-nautilus-under-openbox/") on how to prevent Naughty Nautilus from taking over the desktop also when e.g. browsing files on a device through the Bluetooth Applet, etc. Brilliant!

Icon theme: Gartoon Redux [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Gartoon+Redux?content=74841](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Gartoon+Redux?content=74841)

Fluxbox theme: Bora Blue

"Wbar" is the dock/launcher on top. "Stalonetray" is the system tray on the top right. Stalonetray is also used to stop maximised apps covering wbar, a common problem amongst wbar/fluxbox users. :)

Verrry nice :)

---

### Post by Yes on 2009-03-02
> **Mark76 said:**
> Is Meh the hip new tiling window manager all the cool kids are using? :p

Yeah man, haven't you heard of it? It's great :)

[QUOTE=dbbolton]Did you have to tweak anything in bash to get those colors in your music player? They look sort of pastel-like. The only colors I can get look really stark.[/quote]

Yeah, I had to set some colors in .Xdefaults.  They change the colors for the entire terminal though, not just ncmpcpp.  I never could get ncmpcpp to look good without changing the .Xdefault colors.

If you'd like them, this is what I have for my colors:

```
! tangoesque scheme
! Black
*color0:      #000000
*color8:      #555753
! Red
*color1:      #ff6565
*color9:      #ff8d8d
! Green
*color2:      #93d44f
*color10:     #c8e7a8
! Yellow
*color3:      #eab93d
*color11:     #ffc123
! Blue
*color4:      #204a87
*color12:     #3465a4
! Mangenta
*color5:      #ce5c00
*color13:     #f57900
! Cyan 
*color6:      #89b6e2
*color14:     #46a4ff
! White
*color7:      #cccccc
*color15:     #ffffff
```

> Like Ubuntu it just works....with Openbox, which can be a bit tricky to setup for newbies.  It appeals to users who have had problems installing/not been able to install Openbox....but who are using an old machine.
It's not just that. I've had Openbox in Ubuntu alongside Gnome for some time, and I don't think it is particularly hard to install (heh, just "sudo apt-get install openbox", I think!) and tweak even without all the smart additional stuff in #!. 

Crunchbang is, as I see it, specially intended neither for old hardware nor for unexperienced users (I am that, too), even though it works well for both, I guess. I think (at least still recently) #! Crunchbang "advertised" itself as a distro that may break down occasionally or even frequently, and that may just make your computer say "Crunch! Bang!" Hardly very appealing for absolute beginners, if they are not especially adventurous!

Personally, I am very fond of #!, my favourite Ubuntu derivative, fast becoming my favourite distro. I find it very well designed in many respects and indeed "user friendly" in a distinctly different sense than standard Ubuntu (or Kubuntu or Xubuntu). I do have a semi-old desktop machine and I am a non-technical user with just some nine months' old relationship with Linux, for the most part with generic Ubuntu.

Nine months often means enough time to give birth to something new and unheard-of... So I actually installed #! already a second time, but not on the same machine (but instead of that, a tinyish spare external HDD to carry along &#8212; and I've plugged it onto my brand-newish laptop too, occasionally, because it's so fast and just works actually better than my standard Ubuntu install...).

**P.S.** Ha, I dug up the actual "advertisement" &#8212; actually a [disclaimer]("http://crunchbanglinux.org/wiki/about"):

> **Disclaimer**

CrunchBang Linux is not recommended for anyone needing a stable system or anyone who is not comfortable running into occasional, even frequent breakage. CrunchBang Linux could possibly make your computer go CRUNCH! BANG!

**P.P.S.** And what's more, in #! I have a light, Openbox-based distro, which *I do not have to tweak at all* if I don't want to or don't have the time and energy (I've put way too much time into it with other distros, but #! works so well and looks so good that I don't feel the need to tweak).  

Oh what a fine fanatic I'm becoming! I've seen the light!

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-03-03
> **Yes said:**
> Yeah man, haven't you heard of it? It's great :)



Yeah, I had to set some colors in .Xdefaults.  They change the colors for the entire terminal though, not just ncmpcpp.  I never could get ncmpcpp to look good without changing the .Xdefault colors.

If you'd like them, this is what I have for my colors:

```
! tangoesque scheme
! Black
*color0:      #000000
*color8:      #555753
! Red
*color1:      #ff6565
*color9:      #ff8d8d
! Green
*color2:      #93d44f
*color10:     #c8e7a8
! Yellow
*color3:      #eab93d
*color11:     #ffc123
! Blue
*color4:      #204a87
*color12:     #3465a4
! Mangenta
*color5:      #ce5c00
*color13:     #f57900
! Cyan 
*color6:      #89b6e2
*color14:     #46a4ff
! White
*color7:      #cccccc
*color15:     #ffffff
```

Could you post your ncmpcpp rc as well? Thanks

### Post by Yes on 2009-03-03
> **dbbolton said:**
> Could you post your ncmpcpp rc as well? Thanks

It's actually .ncmpcpp/config (unless we're talking about different files). Here it is -

```
####################################################
## this is example configuration file, copy it to ##
## ~/.ncmpcpp/config and set up your preferences  ##
####################################################
#
##### connection settings #####
#
## set it in order to make tag editor and renaming files work properly
#
mpd_music_dir = "/var/lib/mpd/music"

mpd_connection_timeout = "5"

mpd_crossfade_time = "5"

#### delays #####

# delay after playlist highlighting will be disabled (0 = don't disable)

playlist_disable_highlight_delay = "1"

# defines how long various messages are supposed to be visible

message_delay_time = "4"

#### song format #####
#
# for song format you can use:
#
# %l - length
# %f - short filename
# %F - full filename
# %a - artist
# %t - title
# %b - album
# %y - year
# %n - track number
# %g - genre
# %c - composer
# %p - performer
# %d - disc
# %C - comment
# %r - begin right align
#
# you can also put them in { } and then it will be displayed
# only if all requested values are available and/or define alternate
# value with { }|{ } eg. {%a - %t}|{%f}
#
# text can also have different color than the main window has,
# eg. if you want length to have other color, write [.color]%t[/color]
#
# available colors:
#
# - black
# - red
# - green
# - yellow
# - blue
# - magenta
# - cyan
# - white
#

song_list_format = "{[.green](%l)[/green] }{%a - }{%t}|{[.white]%r%b[/white]}"

song_library_format = "{%n - }{%t}|{%f}"

media_library_album_format = "{(%y) }%b"

tag_editor_album_format = "{(%y) }%b"

browser_playlist_prefix = "[.red]playlist[/red] "

selected_item_prefix = "[.magenta]"

selected_item_suffix = "[/magenta]"

# colors are not supported for below veriables

song_status_format = "{(%l) }{%a - }{%t}|{%f}"

song_window_title_format = "{%a - }{%t}|{%f}"

#### columns settings #####
#
# syntax of song columns list format is "column column etc."
#
# - syntax for each column is:
#
# (width of column in %)[column's color]{displayed tag}
#
# - color is optional (if it's not present, default window color will be used)
#

song_columns_list_format = "(8)[green]{l} (28)[cyan]{a} (28){b} (50)[red]{t}"

#### various settings #####

playlist_display_mode = "columns" (classic/columns)

incremental_seeking = "yes"

seek_time = "1"

autocenter_mode = "no"

repeat_one_mode = "no"

media_library_left_column = "a" (possible values: a,y,g,c,p, legend above)

default_find_mode = "wrapped" (wrapped/normal)

default_space_mode = "add" (add/select)

default_tag_editor_left_col = "albums" (albums/dirs)

default_tag_editor_pattern = "%n - %t"

header_visibility = "yes"

statusbar_visibility = "yes"

fancy_scrolling = "yes"

follow_now_playing_lyrics = "no"

ncmpc_like_songs_adding = "no" (enabled - add/remove, disabled - always add)

enable_window_title = "yes"

#### colors definitions #####

colors_enabled = "yes"

empty_tag_color = "cyan"

header_window_color = "default"

volume_color = "default"

state_line_color = "default"

state_flags_color = "default"

main_window_color = "yellow"

color1 = "white"

color2 = "green"

main_window_highlight_color = "yellow"

progressbar_color = "default"

statusbar_color = "default"

active_column_color = "red"

window_border_color = "green"

active_window_border = "red"
```

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-03-03
> **Yes said:**
> It's actually .ncmpcpp/config (unless we're talking about different files). Here it is -

```
####################################################
## this is example configuration file, copy it to ##
## ~/.ncmpcpp/config and set up your preferences  ##
####################################################
#
##### connection settings #####
#
## set it in order to make tag editor and renaming files work properly
#
mpd_music_dir = "/var/lib/mpd/music"

mpd_connection_timeout = "5"

mpd_crossfade_time = "5"

#### delays #####

# delay after playlist highlighting will be disabled (0 = don't disable)

playlist_disable_highlight_delay = "1"

# defines how long various messages are supposed to be visible

message_delay_time = "4"

#### song format #####
#
# for song format you can use:
#
# %l - length
# %f - short filename
# %F - full filename
# %a - artist
# %t - title
# %b - album
# %y - year
# %n - track number
# %g - genre
# %c - composer
# %p - performer
# %d - disc
# %C - comment
# %r - begin right align
#
# you can also put them in { } and then it will be displayed
# only if all requested values are available and/or define alternate
# value with { }|{ } eg. {%a - %t}|{%f}
#
# text can also have different color than the main window has,
# eg. if you want length to have other color, write [.color]%t[/color]
#
# available colors:
#
# - black
# - red
# - green
# - yellow
# - blue
# - magenta
# - cyan
# - white
#

song_list_format = "{[.green](%l)[/green] }{%a - }{%t}|{[.white]%r%b[/white]}"

song_library_format = "{%n - }{%t}|{%f}"

media_library_album_format = "{(%y) }%b"

browser_playlist_prefix = "[.red]playlist[/red] "

selected_item_prefix = "[.magenta]"

song_status_format = "{(%l) }{%a - }{%t}|{%f}"

song_window_title_format = "{%a - }{%t}|{%f}"

#### columns settings #####
#
# syntax of song columns list format is "column column etc."
#
# - syntax for each column is:
#
# (width of column in %)[column's color]{displayed tag}
#
# - color is optional (if it's not present, default window color will be used)
#

song_columns_list_format = "(8)[green]{l} (28)[cyan]{a} (28){b} (50)[red]{t}"

#### various settings #####

playlist_display_mode = "columns" (classic/columns)

incremental_seeking = "yes"

seek_time = "1"

autocenter_mode = "no"

repeat_one_mode = "no"

media_library_left_column = "a" (possible values: a,y,g,c,p, legend above)

default_find_mode = "wrapped" (wrapped/normal)

default_space_mode = "add" (add/select)

default_tag_editor_left_col = "albums" (albums/dirs)

default_tag_editor_pattern = "%n - %t"

header_visibility = "yes"

statusbar_visibility = "yes"

fancy_scrolling = "yes"

follow_now_playing_lyrics = "no"

ncmpc_like_songs_adding = "no" (enabled - add/remove, disabled - always add)

enable_window_title = "yes"

#### colors definitions #####

colors_enabled = "yes"

empty_tag_color = "cyan"

header_window_color = "default"

volume_color = "default"

state_line_color = "default"

state_flags_color = "default"

main_window_color = "yellow"

color1 = "white"

color2 = "green"

main_window_highlight_color = "yellow"

progressbar_color = "default"

statusbar_color = "default"

active_column_color = "red"

window_border_color = "green"

active_window_border = "red"
```
I trust your judgment. I've only used the program a couple times, and that was awhile ago :D

### Post by Rydgel on 2009-03-04
@sujoy:

The vim colorsheme is Molokai : [http://github.com/tomasr/dotfiles/blob/master/.vim/colors/molokai.vim](http://github.com/tomasr/dotfiles/blob/master/.vim/colors/molokai.vim)
You need a 256 colors term or gvim.
And here is the .Xdefaults, a work from @Daisuke_Aramaki :
```
*background:       #222222
*foreground:       #cacaca
!black
*color0:           #080808
*color8:           #505050
!red
*color1:           #b04020
*color9:           #dd4010
!green
*color2:           #afd700
*color10:          #daff30
!yellow
*color3:           #f7cf0a
*color11:          #fce70d
!blue
*color4:           #3060aa
*color12:          #6099dd
!magenta
*color5:           #d6156c
*color13:          #fe4365
!cyan
*color6:           #a0c2de
*color14:          #c9dee8
!white
*color7:           #808080
*color15:          #b0b0b0
```

---

### Post by sujoy on 2009-03-04
> **Rydgel said:**
> @sujoy:

The vim colorsheme is Molokai : [http://github.com/tomasr/dotfiles/blob/master/.vim/colors/molokai.vim](http://github.com/tomasr/dotfiles/blob/master/.vim/colors/molokai.vim)
You need a 256 colors term or gvim.
And here is the .Xdefaults, a work from @Daisuke_Aramaki :
```
*background:       #222222
*foreground:       #cacaca
!black
*color0:           #080808
*color8:           #505050
!red
*color1:           #b04020
*color9:           #dd4010
!green
*color2:           #afd700
*color10:          #daff30
!yellow
*color3:           #f7cf0a
*color11:          #fce70d
!blue
*color4:           #3060aa
*color12:          #6099dd
!magenta
*color5:           #d6156c
*color13:          #fe4365
!cyan
*color6:           #a0c2de
*color14:          #c9dee8
!white
*color7:           #808080
*color15:          #b0b0b0
```

thank you so much :)

### Post by sertse on 2009-03-05
Not much has changed screenshot wise since my post on top of page 2. Seen here - [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6818154&postcount=11](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6818154&postcount=11) 

However I want to show everyone something... I have now got an almost seamless startup from boot to desktop. :D :D

First, the Usplash theme: Sunset Usplash (Colors) 

[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Sunset+Usplash+(Colors)?content=98003](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Sunset+Usplash+(Colors)?content=98003) 

You need to get Usplash Smooth first: 

[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Ubuntu+Usplash+Smooth?content=93386](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Ubuntu+Usplash+Smooth?content=93386)

Then, the matching GDM theme: Sunset

[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Sunset?content=85709](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Sunset?content=85709)

You know how there's a moment after you login from GDM and before your desktop appears that your screen shows a single color, while it loads?  

Follow this guide: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=753261](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=753261) It shows you how to set an image as your background during that process. I set it to show my desktop background, which follows the same theme as my GDM and Usplash, making login seamless 

The desktop background, Sureal Sunset can be found here. 

[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Surreal+Sunset+%2BBlue+%2BHuman+Colors?content=85183](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Surreal+Sunset+%2BBlue+%2BHuman+Colors?content=85183) 

The end result is just amazing, haha. There is only a half second flicker as it switches from Usplash to GDM. The really speculator part is that gdm to desktop is *completely* smoooth. No flicker, just one flowing transition as goes GDM -> Loading image (same background as my desktop) ->  Desktop. 

I think I'm ranting, but I a bit giddy at how well it turned out. :D :D

---

Got bored, drastically redid my desktop. The most drastic part was upgrading to XFCE 4.6.

Clean on left, dirty on right. Click either for big.

[[IMG]http://img24.imageshack.us/img24/3562/flygonxfce46screenie.th.png[/IMG]](http://img24.imageshack.us/my.php?image=flygonxfce46screenie.png) [[IMG]http://img18.imageshack.us/img18/6671/flygonxfce46screeniedir.th.png[/IMG]](http://img18.imageshack.us/my.php?image=flygonxfce46screeniedir.png)

Details:

DE: XFCE 4.6 Final
GTK: GlassyBleu
XFWM: Daloa
Icons: iComity
Firefox: HP Firefox Theme (came with GlassyBleu)
Fonts: Terminus Bold (terminal, window borders), MiscFixed (conky), Lucida Console (clock - needed a monospace font for it), LuzSans Book (everything else)
Wallpaper: Polarlight (from Interfacelift)

Panel arrangement is as follows (from left): Main menu (Flygon icon), Places, Firefox, Terminal, Rhythmbox, VLC, Trash, Verve, seperator (expanded), Icon list, Notification area, Pager, Weather, Mixer, Show desktop, Screenshot, Orage, Logout button

### Post by J@n on 2009-03-08
Ok, so I just had to show off my desktop. It took me some time to get it just right but I got it in the end.

Theme: Custom
[LIST]
[*]Controls: Human-Clearlooks
[*]Window Border: Glossy
[*]Icons: black-white 2 Gloss _[http://www.gnome-look.org]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/black-white+2+Gloss?content=72621")_
[/LIST]
Wallpaper: Gray-1024x768 _[http://www.desktopwallpaper.in]("http://www.desktopwallpaper.in/view/gray-1024x768.jpg")_

Conky: conkyrc file compiled from different samples at _[http://conky.sourceforge.net]("http://conky.sourceforge.net")_ specifically _[this example]("http://conky.sourceforge.net/conkyrc-ke49")_. Had to tinker with the colors but that was easy

_[Cairo-Dock 2.0.0-beta2.1]("http://www.cairo-dock.org/index.php")_. Replaced default icons with icons from black-white 2 Gloss

Hope you like it;)

Greetz,

J@n

### Post by John.Michael.Kane on 2009-03-08
> **el mariachi said:**
> how are vim themes applied?

If I am not mistaken, to install a Vim color theme/scheme, download the theme/scheme from the site you seen it on, and place it in ~/.vim/colors/. 

You can then enable it in your ~/.vimrc file with the following line:

colorscheme (scheme name here)

However, if you want to edit default themes to fit your needs.

You can copy the file from /usr/share/vim/vim71/colors/name.vim to the desktop and make your modifications.

You would have to change the line 22 from let g:colors_name="new name here" to the name of  the new Vim color theme. Then make your changes to any of the of the other lines that you want to edit. When finished save the file with a new name that matched the name that you gave the scheme inside the file.

Hope that helps.

The icons to the right of the address bar are bookmark icons.  You just remove the name from the properties so that only the icon is displayed.

As for the menu bar, I'm guessing that he is using an extension or other about:config setting to hide it.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-03-09

Mac fonts, Mac cursor theme, Mac wall. If I'm not careful I'm going to start drinking lattes and buy a hybrid. :p

Also gave Ristretto another shot since Gimmage hasn't been updated in about 2 years and I don't know how long it's going to continue to be usable. Ristretto is down-right elegant, now. None of that buggy behaviour it had about a year ago. Only drawback is scrollwheel behaviour; Gimmage used the scrollwheel as, well, a *scroll*wheel until you held down Ctrl, at which point it modified it's behaviour to zoom. In Ristretto, Ctrl or no Ctrl, the scrollwheel zooms. :/

Edit: spoke too soon. Ristretto still can't pan to save it's life.


Also a question for the gtkrc hackers out there: is there a window match for the Gnome/Xfce notification popups so I can change their colours?

own_window_title conkyrss

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont Segoe Semibold:size=6
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no

draw_outline no
default_outline_color 2525ff
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color0 ffffff
color1 cfdfdf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 0a0a0a #111111 #1a1a1a #720000
color4 0a0a0a #101010

own_window yes
own_window_colour 080808
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_left
gap_x -2
gap_y 20
minimum_size 1440 0

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-03-11
> **sujoy said:**
> [[IMG]http://th06.deviantart.com/fs43/300W/f/2009/070/e/a/theMarchToGnome_by_binarycodes.png[/IMG]]("http://binarycodes.deviantart.com/art/theMarchToGnome-115561943")

any idea on how to reduce the notification area icon size?

You can manipulate gnome-panel's spacing with xthickness/ythickness in your gtkrc, which will affect notification icons (assuming your icon theme has defined those icons as scalable in index.theme). Think gtk-icon-sizes is depreciated; it doesn't work in Xfce 4.6 anymore, at least.

### Post by Agent69 on 2009-03-12
> **C!oud said:**
> How is OpenBSD? As a NetBSD user I've been looking to properly try it for quite some time.

I used to use NetBSD back in the 1.6 days, and I would probably be using it now, but for some reason I can't get my USB keyboard to work once the installer is fully booted. Hopefully, 5.0 will fix that.

OpenBSD is pretty similar to NetBSD most respects. The only thing that is more difficult in OpenBSD in the disk partitioning software, but once you get past that, all is pretty familiar.

### Post by ayoli on 2009-03-13
> **mpsii said:**
> Is the info thing in the terminal a script or did you just type it all in?
Yes, it is a script, it requires indent and scrot and you may need to adjust some parts :
```
#!/bin/bash

# screenshot dir
ssdir="$HOME/"
# screenshot description
ssdesc="$HOME/"
# screenshot format
ss=`date +%d%m%Y`.png

# Extra hdd details?
hdddetails=0
# Use comments file?
comments=0
# Automatically grab gnome theme info
autognome=1

#############################
# begin output

echo

#echo "Distro:         `cat /etc/*release`"
#############################
#try one of the two below or edit for your distro
#source /etc/*release
source /etc/lsb-release
#
echo "$DISTRIB_ID $DISTRIB_RELEASE $DISTRIB_CODENAME, kernel $(uname -r)"

#echo "Uptime:         `uptime |cut --delimiter=" " -f 2`"
echo " "
echo "HARDWARE :"
echo "&#9472;——————————————————————————————————————————&#9472;——————————————————————————&#9472;"
echo "CPU:           `grep -m 1 "model name" /proc/cpuinfo|cut --delimiter=":" -f 2`" 
#echo "Bogomips:      `grep "bogomips" /proc/cpuinfo|cut --delimiter=":" -f 2` bogomips"
#echo --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

let memtotal=`grep "MemTotal" /proc/meminfo|cut -c 12-22|indent -i0`/1024
#echo "Memory Total:   $memtotal mb"
let memfree=`grep "MemFree" /proc/meminfo|cut -c 12-22|indent -i0`/1024
let memcache=`grep "Cached" /proc/meminfo|cut -c 12-22|indent -i0`
let memcache=$memcache/1024
let memfreetotal=$memfree+$memcache
echo "Memory Free:    $memfreetotal mb    Memory Total:   $memtotal mb"

#echo "Graphics:       `grep "Product" /proc/fb0/vbe_info|cut --delimiter=" " -f 5`" 
echo "Graphics:	`lspci |grep 00:02.1 |cut --delimiter=" " -f 4,5,6,7,8,9`"
#cat /proc/driver/nvidia/version
echo " "
echo "DESIGN :"
echo "&#9472;——————————————————————————————————————————&#9472;——————————————————————————&#9472;"
if [ $autognome == 1 ]; then
  echo "GTK2:           		`gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/gtk_theme`"
  #echo "Metacity:                       `gconftool-2 --get /apps/metacity/general/theme`"
  echo -e "Emerald:	                $(grep description $HOME/.emerald/theme/theme.ini |cut -c 13-)";
  echo "Icons:          		`gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/icon_theme`"
#  echo "Titlebar Font:      		`gconftool-2 --get /apps/metacity/general/titlebar_font`"
  echo "Wallpaper: 	                `gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/background/picture_filename  |cut -d / -f 5`"
  echo "Application Font:  		`gconftool-2 --get /desktop/gnome/interface/font_name`"
  echo "Terminal Font:  		`gconftool-2 --get /apps/gnome-terminal/profiles/Default/font`"
fi
sleep 2
`scrot -d 6 $ss`
echo
exit 0
```
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Best one yet. I'm curious as to how you got that top border on conky.
Thank you :) The conky top border is only an hr :
```
${voffset -7}${color 444444}${hr 1}
```

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-03-13
> **Giant Speck said:**
> I'd do it myself, but I don't like the fact I can't use GNOME icon themes with KDE.

You can use most Gnome icon themes with KDE. In fact, most of the icon themes I have installed are Gnome themes. They both go by the freedesktop.org icon naming spec now. It's usually just a matter of changing the inherits line in the index.theme file to Oxygen.

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-03-14
> **odda said:**

Thanks. :)

Most of the details can be found [here]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Meno?content=100738"). As for the taskbar, if you're referring to the tasklist, it's the [stasks plasmoid]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/STasks?content=99739"). The other plasmoids are lancelot, playwolf, system tray, and the digital clock.

### Post by tech13 on 2009-03-14
:KS[COLOR="Navy"][SIZE="4"]I have for you all, a gift, of font.[/SIZE][/COLOR]:KS

[B][SIZE="4"]If you would like to make your own font you require

- Printer/Scanner
or
- Tablet[/SIZE][/B]

go to [SIZE="5"][www.yourfonts.com]("http://www.yourfonts.com")[/SIZE] and print out the template, read the instructions on how to fill out the template, use something a bit thicker than a pen, but smaller than a felt tip marker, one of those very fine tipped liquid pens should do the trick (although they tend to leak into the paper), What I did was wrote it in pencil first then wrote overtop in ink, then erased the pencil. 

Upload the font to the site and it will generate a true type font for you, with your own name/copyright on it. It's custom, unique and no one else will have it, check out the samples too, some look nice (too bad we can't download them)

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
**Edit: **I decided I will display my horrible penmanship for you all to see my font I made... It's bad simply because I can't write... years of computer use will do this to you unfortunately.

[[IMG]http://img14.imageshack.us/img14/5537/screenshot22.th.png[/IMG]](http://img14.imageshack.us/img14/5537/screenshot22.png)

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-03-14
Just got myself a *Logitech Cordless Desktop Wave* which includes an LX8 laser mouse. I went for this model primarily because the mouse had a tilt-wheel. Unfortunately, whoever wrote the *nix driver decided to set the tilt-buttons to emulate the left/right keyboard arrow keys, rather than actually horizontally scroll. :(

On the plus-side, the mouse has, "forward", and, "backwards", buttons on either side which I'm *loving*, having assigned forwards to activate the shift-switcher and back to activate expo.

[img]http://img11.imageshack.us/img11/2694/megatmb.png[/img]

Shits all over keyboard shortcuts and hot-corners.

### Post by billgoldberg on 2009-03-16
> **Giant Speck said:**
> I'd post a screenshot right now, but I really REALLLLLLY screwed up Compiz and I can't figure out how to fix it. ](*,) :cry:

```
sudo apt-get autoremove compiz -- purge
```

and then reinstall it and all the plugins that got removed.

:p:p

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-03-16
> **billgoldberg said:**
> ```
sudo apt-get autoremove compiz -- purge
```

and then reinstall it and all the plugins that got removed.

:p:p

In my experience, purging has never deleted user-specific configurations (ie. in $HOME). Unless Speck was editing the compiz startup script as root or something equally system-wide, all he should need to do is kill GDM (assuming he's set compiz to automatically load) and rm -r $HOME/.config/compiz

---

### Post by Islington on 2009-03-16
> **Netsu said:**
> I was once trying to find out how to texture windows but found nothing, can you post your gtk theme or a link to some other theme with pixmap window textures? I guess it would be the easiest way for me to learn how to implement it :)

Pixmap theme engine has 0 documentation that I have ever found. even after talking to Cimi. As such I am learning to make my wood gtk based on Mirav2. Other good ones are NewWave and Dust(?). Gnome-look has all three. I will release mine when it isn't put together with duct tape.

---

### Post by Agent69 on 2009-03-16
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> i think i need to know more about that.

Many X clients support a -geometry switch which allows for setting window position and size when the client starts. One of the notable exceptions to this is Firefox, although it does offer command line switches for setting height and width.

Running without a window manager is light but it also means that you can't move or raise/lower windows. It also means that sloppy focus is always in effect. And some applications have problems working without a window manager present.

---

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2009-03-16
> **Agent69 said:**
> Many X clients support a -geometry switch which allows for setting window position and size when the client starts. One of the notable exceptions to this is Firefox, although it does offer command line switches for setting height and width.

Running without a window manager is light but it also means that you can't move or raise/lower windows. It also means that sloppy focus is always in effect. And some applications have problems working without a window manager present.

thanks for the explanation.

---

### Post by Agent69 on 2009-03-16
> **Daisuke_Aramaki said:**
> One question mate. Are you able to get all the features of S10 working with OpenBSD, like wireless, hotkeys, acpi etc?

The built it wireless adapter doesn't work with OpenBSD, so I had to use a USB ethernet adapter. I have learned that it is possible to replace the built in wireless card with an Intel 5100, which is supported, but I haven't decided if I want to do it yet.

I don't know about ASPI or hotkeys. The only thing I did for the laptop that I don't normally do was enable Apmd and set it for cool running mode. It seemed to down clock the CPU to 800mhz, so I guess that works.

---

I've wanted to do a very HL2-esque theme for a while but I'm terrible at creating colour palettes. I feel compelled to rip off yours...

---

### Post by raul_ on 2009-03-16
> **interllect said:**
> Can i ask you what svn is and are they only in kdemod?

tia

SVN packages are development versions of programs. They are highly error prone while showing all the new stuff the developers are working on (new features, artwork, etc). You should be able to get them for Ubuntu too (you'll have to Google that since I haven't used Ubuntu in about 2 years), but I don't really recommend them, unless you're that eager to have a glimpse of the future.

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-03-17
> **izizzle said:**
> Is there any way to achieve transparency without having the desktop effects enabled? BTW, is it the KDE Desktop Effects or Compiz? 

Thanks.

P.S: Eightmillion I love your KDE Theme/Setup. Nice 'n clean :D

Thanks. You can have transparent widgets without compositing, but to get a transparent panel, you have to be running a compositing window manager. It doesn't matter what that window manager is, as long as it supports compositing.

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2009-03-20
> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> Pardon my offtopic'ness, but how did you achieve that firefox setup?  Is that a user chrome change or a series of settings?  Any chance of getting a copy if it is a chrome change?

no chrome change. the 'tiny menu' extension reduces all that "file, edit, etc." mess down to just 'menu. i moved the url bar and bookmarks toolbar menu up to the top bar and just use the favicons to identify the bookmarks and then just get rid of the bookmarks and navigation bars.


> **dbbolton said:**
> Is that xfwm4?

indeedy!

### Post by lzfy on 2009-03-21
> **TomTwice said:**
> Where can I get the icons? And what widget style are you using. And to top it all off, what are the exact details of your colour scheme?

Looks totally awesome!

Thanks man :) The style is bespin and the used preset is 'Lightroom'. To get the preset just run the command 
     ```
svn co https://cloudcity.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/cloudcity 
```

That will download the source of the style but also some really cool config files in the /presets folder. Plasma theme is Aya. The icon theme is iKons but I haven't updated it yet. Will do it soon.

> Check his signature, thanks for the awesome port of eikon, lzfy.


You're welcome ;)

### Post by sertse on 2009-03-21
> **cardinals_fan said:**
> What is it?

You can probably see it from the screenshot; its the xfce4-session-logout menu appearing inside fluxbox. 

Strictly speaking, I'm using xfce, not fluxbox. That is what I choose when I logged in. It just that I did a few edits to xfce session that commented out all the xfce things it usually loads up (xfwm, xfdesktop, xfce-panel etc), instead only loading my fluxbox startup script. 

What I get is session saving and as you can see from the screenshot, the xfce quit menu. In pure fluxbox, you either need to enter your password to shutdown/reboot, or by editing sudoers which opens the possibility of accidentally shutting down the system on a misclick on the menu,

---

### Post by cardinals_fan on 2009-03-21
> **sertse said:**
> You can probably see it from the screenshot; its the xfce4-session-logout menu appearing inside fluxbox. 

Strictly speaking, I'm using xfce, not fluxbox. That is what I choose when I logged in. It just that I did a few edits to xfce session that commented out all the xfce things it usually loads up (xfwm, xfdesktop, xfce-panel etc), instead only loading my fluxbox startup script. 

What I get is session saving and as you can see from the screenshot, the xfce quit menu. In pure fluxbox, you either need to enter your password to shutdown/reboot, or by editing sudoers which opens the possibility of accidentally shutting down the system on a misclick on the menu,
Actually, the Xfce quit menu is available with xfce4-session-logout.  It doesn't matter if you're using Xfce - it will still work.

---

### Post by sertse on 2009-03-22
xfce4-session-logout needs xfce4-session to work. 

However, if you start xfce4-session after a fluxbox login. xfce4-session-logout doesn't work, (Though the rest of xfce4-session does, oddly). It'll spew out a session manager not running error of some sort..

It does work if you login as a xfce session and fluxbox is started after xfce session.

That's what I'm experiencing from tinkering..., (this is on sidux, don't know if it matters though)

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-03-22
> **the8thstar said:**
> This is a Gnome Applet that I use to type French letters because the keyboard I have on this laptop is QWERTY (US). The applet is "**Character Palette**".
When I need to type in French (pretty rare these days), I use a custom palette (Right-click > Preferences > Add) rather than the default ones, because they have a lot of characters that I never use. For example, a 'common' palette and a 'complete' one:

```
àâçéèêîôûù
```
```
   âàçéêèëîïôûùüÿÂÀÇÉÊÈËÎÏÔÛÙÜ&#376;°&#8364;
```

Stats:
```
own_window_title conkystats

use_xft yes
xftfont LucidaMacBold:size=7
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color ff0000
draw_outline yes
default_outline_color 151515
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color1 cfcfcf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 909090

own_window yes
own_window_colour 080808 #121212
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_middle
gap_x 5
gap_y -2
minimum_size 900 0

TEXT

> **Giant Speck said:**
> Lucky you in both cases.  I'm sitting at 218.5 MB of RAM usage using Swiftfox 3.0.4pre.

Are there any *easy* instructions out there for installing Firefox 3.1b3 on Ubuntu?

Don't compile it yourself, install it locally and just copy firefox.desktop to your .local directory and edit the exec path in a text editor?

It's what I do; untar the pre-compiled binary to $HOME/programmes/firefox/ and redirect the .desktop launcher to that location.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-03-24
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> 
Don't compile it yourself, install it locally and just copy firefox.desktop to your .local directory and edit the exec path in a text editor?

It's what I do; untar the pre-compiled binary to $HOME/programmes/firefox/ and redirect the .desktop launcher to that location.

What about doing this?

> 
Go to System > Administration > Software Sources, to the Third-Party Software tab and add this repository:

 [FONT=Courier New]deb [http://ppa.launchpad.net/fta/ubuntu](http://ppa.launchpad.net/fta/ubuntu) intrepid main

[/FONT]click on Close, open a terminal and type: [FONT=Courier New]sudo apt-get update
[/FONT] 
 Then, go to System > Administration > Synaptic Package Manager and search for Firefox, select version 3.1 to be installed (it will also install additional files). After install is complete, open your file browser (because Firefox 3.1 does not create a shortcut) and navigate to [FONT=Courier New]/usr/lib/firefox-3.1b2[/FONT]. To open FIrefox 3.1, double click [FONT=Courier New]firefox-3.1[/FONT].
 To make a shortcut, simply drag [FONT=Courier New]firefox-3.1[/FONT] to one of your panels.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-03-24
IIRC, the password file will only work in the correct profile. Copying it to a new profile will just result in it being over-ridden. I got around this by, perhaps unwisely, letting foxmarks backup both my bookmarks and my passwords and then installing foxmarks in the new profile. Your other option is to copy your current profile (ie create a backup) and try using the same profile with 3.1 permanently. If things aren't borked, you should be able to get away with the old profile.

My problem was taking a 3.1 profile and trying to use it with an older firefox build. The profile gets totally screwed.

---

### Post by xc3RnbFO8P on 2009-03-24
> So you're intentionally using the theme without the required engine?
Yes

### Post by Fixel on 2009-03-24

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-03-24
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> which wm is that? is that compiz by itself? how does that happen?It's compiz + emerald decorator in an otherwise normal Xfce 4.6 environment. I'd use Xfwm4 (which shames compiz in a pure basic WM race) but I've become dependent upon Expo, full-screen zoom and the shift-switcher.

> **Fixel said:**
> True that. But one thing I haven't been able to figure out is how to make compiz ignore the binds (middle-click) for when I'm using programs like Firefox.

This makes closing/opening (new) tabs a pain.

That shouldn't happen. I'd suggest falling back to another WM, renaming .config/compiz to .config/compiz_bkp and testing compiz in a stock configuration. If it still happens, then something weird is up.

If all else fails, disable whichever plugin wants to use mouse button 2 and make sure browser.tabs.opentabfor.middleclick is set to true in about:config.

---

### Post by Fixel on 2009-03-24

I really don't know what's wrong. The stock config method didn't work either. I'm at a total loss.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-03-24
I'm guessing you've assigned the middle-click function to zoom-out & freely rotate the cube? What happens when you don't assign mouse button 2 to do anything in compiz?

And no, it's not normal for that to happen. I expereinced similarly weird behaviour when I tried the proprietary HIDPoint mouse/keyboard driver a few weeks back. Not using those?

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-03-24
> **Felliph3 said:**
> I pasted the conky stuff and it loads for a sec then its gone and I get these errors if I run it from the terminal. Im not a linux newbie but I dont program and some stuff is complicated for me.
felliphe@felliphe-laptop:~$ conky
Conky: statfs '/media/windows_drive': No such file or directory
Conky: statfs '/media/shared_drive': No such file or directory
Conky: statfs '/fakelol/': No such file or directory
Conky: forked to background, pid is 7856
felliphe@felliphe-laptop:~$ 
Conky: desktop window (14000a8) is subwindow of root window (c3)
Conky: window type - dock
Conky: drawing to created window (0x3a00001)
Conky: drawing to double buffer
Conky: statfs '/fakelol/': No such file or directory
Conky: statfs '/media/shared_drive': No such file or directory
Conky: statfs '/media/windows_drive': No such file or directory
sh: iheart8mil.sh: not found
sh: iheart8mil2.sh: not found


Any ideas? Thanks man!

My whole conky file

The drive entries are HIS drives...you need to edit to drives you actually own or remove the entry, conky can't find drives you don't have.

You probably don't have the fonts either, LucidaMacBold or Segoe.  Never use someone else's conky scripts without going through and editing entries to suit your desktop environment or you end up with issues.

```

> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> The drive entries are HIS drives...you need to edit to drives you actually own or remove the entry, conky can't find drives you don't have.

You probably don't have the fonts either, LucidaMacBold or Segoe.  Never use someone else's conky scripts without going through and editing entries to suit your desktop environment or you end up with issues.

Even if there's stuff missing, it shouldn't crash. What version of Conky are you running? Hopefully the Jaunty version doesn't get finicky about dead-end fsbars. I need those.

Remove the ${execi xxx.sh} sections and see if it works.

Edit: Hold on, you've tried to stick both my conky configs together. They need to be separate and loaded as separate instances of conky.

Put the original .conkyrc text in $HOME/.conkyrc, put conkyrss1 in $HOME/.conky/conkyrss1, then put the following text in $HOME/bin/conkyall.sh:
```
#bin/sh

sleep 1

conky
conky -c .conky/conkyrss1
```

And make the .sh shell script executable.

Then if you want conky to automatically load when you login, create an autostart entry and point it to the script.

### Post by Agent69 on 2009-03-25
> **dbbolton said:**
> I have seen people on this forum refer to Gnome+Compiz as "minimal". If you want to get REALLY minimal, you should use twm or tinywm

...or no X at all.

In Arch x64, the Twm executable comes in at 166kb and Evilwm executable comes in at 30kb, which is probably not too surprising to anyone who has read both Evilwm and Twm manpages. Plus, Evilwm does not litter my home directory with dotfiles (in fact, it doesn't use any).

I did, at one time, run without a window manager but I discovered that Firefox has issues displaying its menus when a window manager is not running.

Here is my Lenovo Ideapad S10 running OpenBSD, Xorg 7.3; Xterm, Xcompmgr, and Xclock with no window manager:

[IMG]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3186/3382574068_baff725ff2.jpg[/IMG]

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-03-26
Decided to try something new with conky. Didn't work: every time the ${cpu} entry jumped between single and double digits, everything flickered, jumped around and bugged out. Apparently overlaying dynamic text values over fs_bars, down/upspeedgraphs, cpugraphs etc, which in-turn overlay fs_bars, set to nonexistent locations to appear as 100% and provide the opaque background for the previous graphs and bars, is too much ${goto} abuse for Conky to handle.

[[IMG]http://img259.imageshack.us/img259/2700/toomuchabuse.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img259.imageshack.us/img259/2700/toomuchabuse.jpg)

---

### Post by Tibuda on 2009-03-26
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Decided to try something new with conky. Didn't work: every time the ${cpu} entry jumped between single and double digits, everything flickered, jumped around and bugged out. Apparently overlaying dynamic text values over fs_bars, down/upspeedgraphs, cpugraphs etc, which in-turn overlay fs_bars, set to nonexistent locations to appear as 100% and provide the opaque background for the previous graphs and bars, is too much ${goto} abuse for Conky to handle.
[Check this]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6823850&postcount=5941"). I used $voffset to keep each bar text in different lines, so they are not tied.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-03-26
> **danielrmt said:**
> [Check this]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6823850&postcount=5941"). I used $voffset to keep each bar text in different lines, so they are not tied.

That's not the problem; there's a bug in conky where if any two objects are too close together (let alone overlapping), any state changes cause minor changes in alignment, requiring considerable redraw. Using ${goto} pretty much does the same thing as starting a new line and using ${voffset}, anyway.

---

### Post by walkerk on 2009-03-26
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> compiz-confusion by itself (what a pain in the asterisks).

[[img]http://xs537.xs.to/xs537/09133/gullsalone652.jpg.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs537&d=09133&f=gullsalone652.jpg)

It grows on you :) Minimilistic look with all the extras should you choose to use them :) 

I personally don't use the Fusion-Icon. Instead, in my compiz start up script I call only compiz... emerald is the window decorator...
```

# Start Compiz & stuff...

nitrogen --set-scaled /home/kevin/themes/wallpaper/96640-simple_blue_widescreen.svg &

sleep 6 && pypanel &

compiz
```

With flattery like that, how could I possibly say no? Oh that's right, I'm an a-hole: NO, HA!
























```
own_window_title conkyrss

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont Segoe Semibold:size=6
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color 2525ff
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 2525ff
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color0 ffffff
color1 cfdfdf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 0a0a0a #111111 #1a1a1a #720000
color4 080808 #101010

own_window yes
own_window_colour 080808
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_left
gap_x -2
gap_y 20
minimum_size 1440 0

TEXT

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-03-29
> **imnotthere said:**
> Very nice tint2-config you got there:) Mind sharing your .tintrc?

Sure thing:

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT2 CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 50
border_color = #000000 50

rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 0 
border_color = #000000 0 

rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 0
border_color = #000000 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_monitor = all
panel_position = bottom left
panel_size = 100% 50
panel_margin = 0 20
panel_padding = 7 -2
font_shadow = 0
panel_background_id = 1

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKBAR
#---------------------------------------------
taskbar_mode = single_monitor
taskbar_padding = 0 0 0
taskbar_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_icon = 1
task_text = 1
task_width = 140
task_centered = 1
task_padding = 6 19
task_font = HeldustryFTVBasic 8
task_font_color = #AEC3D9 100
task_active_font_color = #DCDCDC 100
task_background_id = 0
task_active_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# SYSTRAYBAR
#---------------------------------------------
#systray_padding = 6 2 2
#systray_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format =%H:%M
time1_font = HeldustryFTVBasic 8
time2_format = 
time2_font = Droid Sans Bold 10
clock_font_color = #DCDCDC 100
clock_padding = 2 10
clock_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify
```

If you have a particularly bright wallpaper you may need/want to adjust the pseudo-transparency levels upward to give the "bar" more of a tint.

#---------------------------------------------
# BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 **50**
border_color = #000000 **50**

Adjust the bolded numbers upwards to increase the tint level, and down to decrease it as needed to achieve the darkness you desire.

---

### Post by imnotthere on 2009-03-30
> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> Sure thing:

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT2 CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 50
border_color = #000000 50

rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 0 
border_color = #000000 0 

rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 0
border_color = #000000 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_monitor = all
panel_position = bottom left
panel_size = 100% 50
panel_margin = 0 20
panel_padding = 7 -2
font_shadow = 0
panel_background_id = 1

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKBAR
#---------------------------------------------
taskbar_mode = single_monitor
taskbar_padding = 0 0 0
taskbar_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_icon = 1
task_text = 1
task_width = 140
task_centered = 1
task_padding = 6 19
task_font = HeldustryFTVBasic 8
task_font_color = #AEC3D9 100
task_active_font_color = #DCDCDC 100
task_background_id = 0
task_active_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# SYSTRAYBAR
#---------------------------------------------
#systray_padding = 6 2 2
#systray_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format =%H:%M
time1_font = HeldustryFTVBasic 8
time2_format = 
time2_font = Droid Sans Bold 10
clock_font_color = #DCDCDC 100
clock_padding = 2 10
clock_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify
```

If you have a particularly bright wallpaper you may need/want to adjust the pseudo-transparency levels upward to give the "bar" more of a tint.

#---------------------------------------------
# BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 **50**
border_color = #000000 **50**

Adjust the bolded numbers upwards to increase the tint level, and down to decrease it as needed to achieve the darkness you desire.

Thank you very much:popcorn:

---
